Fifty-five thousand (55,000) in Roman numerals is "LV" which stands for 55, not "Capitol." The correct statement should be written as "Capitol LV." However, if you're looking to express the number fifty-five thousand using Roman numerals correctly, it would actually be represented as "DXXXV," since there is no standard way to directly represent thousands in Roman numerals. Roman numerals typically do not include a concept of 'thousand' and are instead used for numbers up to three (III). For large numbers like 55,000, the Romans would have used combinations of smaller values (like "D" for 5000) but not a direct symbol.

Capital: Capitol. In English, the word "Capitol" refers to a building where a legislative body of a republic, state, or country meets. It is often confused with "capital," which means the city that serves as the seat of government for an entire country or region. However, in some contexts, such as in the United States, "Capitol" specifically refers to the building where Congress meets (the Capitol Building). The distinction between these terms can vary based on regional and political usage. If you're referring to a generic legislative building, it might be more appropriate to use "capital." If you're discussing the specific building in Washington D.C., then "Capitol" is the correct term.

Dynamic splinting is an orthopedic technique used primarily when there is significant soft tissue swelling around a fracture site, which might otherwise restrict healing due to constriction.
